<dt class="glossary" id="aa6061" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">AA6061</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/6061_aluminium_alloy" title="6061 aluminium alloy">6061 aluminium alloy</a></span></p>
Aluminium alloy used for manufacture of new diving cylinders exclusively since mid 1988 as it is not susceptible to <a href="/wiki/Sustained_load_cracking" title="Sustained load cracking">sustained load cracking</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Harlow_1999_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harlow_1999-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PSI_2016_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PSI_2016-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="aa6351" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">AA6351</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Aluminium_alloy#Wrought_alloys" title="Aluminium alloy">Aluminium alloy#Wrought alloys</a></span></p>
Aluminium alloy 6351 is subject to <a href="/wiki/Sustained_load_cracking" title="Sustained load cracking">sustained load cracking</a> and requires periodical <span title="See entry on this page at § eddy current test" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#eddy_current_test" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G">eddy current testing</a></span> to identify crack development at an early stage.<sup id="cite_ref-Harlow_1999_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harlow_1999-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Not used for new cylinder manufacture since 1988, but many cylinders of this alloy are still in service.<sup id="cite_ref-PSI_2016_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PSI_2016-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="ablj" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">ABLJ</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#adjustable_buoyancy_life_jacket"><span title="See entry on this page at § adjustable buoyancy life jacket" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">adjustable buoyancy life jacket</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="absolute_pressure" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">absolute pressure</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Pressure_measurement#Absolute,_gauge_and_differential_pressures_-_zero_reference" title="Pressure measurement">Pressure measurement#Absolute, gauge and differential pressures - zero reference</a></span></p>
Total static pressure at the reference point: Pressure relative to vacuum.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="acd" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">ACD</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#auto-closure_device"><span title="See entry on this page at § auto-closure device" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">auto-closure device</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="a-clamp_adaptor" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">A-clamp adaptor</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <span title="See entry on this page at § yoke adaptor" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z#yoke_adaptor" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: T–Z">yoke adaptor</a></span></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="a-clamp_fitting" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">A-clamp fitting</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="a-clamp_valve" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">A-clamp valve</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <span title="See entry on this page at § yoke fitting" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z#yoke_fitting" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: T–Z">yoke fitting</a></span>, and <a href="#cGA_850"><span title="See entry on this page at § CGA 850" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">CGA 850</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="active_addition" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">active addition</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Rebreather#Active_addition_semi-closed_circuit" title="Rebreather">Rebreather#Active addition semi-closed circuit</a></span></p>
System for semi-closed circuit rebreather feed gas addition in which gas is added to the breathing circuit by a mechanism, regardless of current volume, and excess gas is vented to keep the loop volume within limits. Compare with <span title="See entry on this page at § passive addition" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#passive_addition" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S">passive addition</a></span></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="activated_carbon" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">activated carbon</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="activated_charcoal" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">activated charcoal</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Activated_carbon" title="Activated carbon">Activated carbon</a></span></p>
A filter medium used to remove oil, water, and odours from breathing gas.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="adas" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">ADAS</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#australian_Diver_Accreditation_Scheme"><span title="See entry on this page at § Australian Diver Accreditation Scheme" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">Australian Diver Accreditation Scheme</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="adci" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">ADCI</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#association_of_Diving_Contractors_International"><span title="See entry on this page at § Association of Diving Contractors International" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">Association of Diving Contractors International</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="adjustable_buoyancy_life_jacket" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">adjustable buoyancy life jacket</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "ABLJ", "Fenzy" , or "horse collar buoyancy compensator"</span></p>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Buoyancy_compensator_(diving)#Adjustable_buoyancy_life_jacket" title="Buoyancy compensator (diving)">Buoyancy compensator (diving)#Adjustable buoyancy life jacket</a></span></p>
An early style of combination  <a href="/wiki/Buoyancy_compensator_(diving)" title="Buoyancy compensator (diving)">buoyancy compensator</a> and inflatable life jacket worn on the chest and round the neck.<sup id="cite_ref-BSAC_Manual_1982_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BSAC_Manual_1982-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="adv" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">ADV</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;<i>See: <a href="#automatic_diluent_valve"><span title="See entry on this page at § automatic diluent valve" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">automatic diluent valve</span></a></i></dd> 
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;<i>See: <a href="#automatic_dump_valve"><span title="See entry on this page at § automatic dump valve" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">automatic dump valve</span></a></i></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="a-frame" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">A-frame</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Part of a <span title="See entry on this page at § launch and recovery system" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O#launch_and_recovery_system" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: H–O">launch and recovery system</a></span>. A gantry or davit for launching and recovering bells, stages, anchors, or large ROVs.<sup id="cite_ref-Bevan_2005_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bevan_2005-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ships_and_Oil_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ships_and_Oil-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Usually deployed by hydraulic rams which swing the frame over the deck or overboard as required. The load is hoisted and lowered by cables from the top of the frame.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="age" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">AGE</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#arterial_gas_embolism"><span title="See entry on this page at § arterial gas embolism" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">arterial gas embolism</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="aggressive_decompression" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">aggressive decompression</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Decompression_practice#Conservatism" title="Decompression practice">Decompression practice#Conservatism</a></span></p>
<a href="/wiki/Decompression_schedule" class="mw-redirect" title="Decompression schedule">Decompression schedule</a> tending to shorter overall decompression time for a given pre-ascent dive profile, accepting increased risk of decompression sickness to reduce the overall ascent time.<sup id="cite_ref-Suunto_Fused_RGBM_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Suunto_Fused_RGBM-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="air_dome" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">air dome</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A section of cave which traps air or other gas at the top. This gas is not directly connected to the atmosphere.<sup id="cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;The upper part of an open <a href="/wiki/Diving_bell" title="Diving bell">diving bell</a> which can be filled with air for divers to breathe.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="air_integration" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">air integration</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Dive_computer#Additional_functionality_and_features" title="Dive computer">Dive computer#Additional functionality and features</a></span></p>
Feature of some <span title="See entry on this page at § dive computer" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#dive_computer" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G">dive computer</a></span>s to measure cylinder pressure  using an integral pressure gauge connected by HP hose to the regulator first stage, or receive data from one or more remote pressure transducers fitted to the HP port of a regulator, and display the pressure on the screen. Other features may also be available using the data.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="airlift" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">airlift</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Airlift_(dredging_device)" title="Airlift (dredging device)">Airlift (dredging device)</a></span></p>
A device based on a steeply rising pipe, used by divers to suck small objects, sand and mud from the sea bed and to transport the resulting debris upwards and away from its source. Air is injected into the lower end of the pipe and the rising bubbles entrain water and cause an upward flow which draws the material from the bottom along.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="airline" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">airline</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="air_line" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">air line</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Surface-supplied_diving#Airline" title="Surface-supplied diving">Surface-supplied diving#Airline</a></span></p>
Simple low pressure hose carrying breathing air from a surface supply to a diver.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="airline_diving" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">airline diving</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "hooka", "hookah"</span></p>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Surface-supplied_diving#Airline" title="Surface-supplied diving">Surface-supplied diving#Airline</a></span></p>
Surface-supplied diving where the breathing air is supplied to the diver by a simple hose. The diver usually breathes through a mouth held <span title="See entry on this page at § demand valve" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#demand_valve" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G">demand valve</a></span>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="air_top" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">air top</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="air_top-up" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">air top-up</dfn></dt> 
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">see: <a href="/wiki/Gas_blending_for_scuba_diving#Air_top-up" title="Gas blending for scuba diving">Gas blending for scuba diving#Air top-up</a></span></p></dd> 
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;Completing a planned breathing gas mix by topping up the cylinder with compressed air to a calculated pressure.<sup id="cite_ref-Oxyhacker_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oxyhacker-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;Topping up a partly used breathing gas mix with compressed air, providing a different mixture which is analysed after the fill.<sup id="cite_ref-Oxyhacker_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oxyhacker-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="algal_bloom" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">algal bloom</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Algal_bloom" title="Algal bloom">Algal bloom</a></span></p>
A rapid increase or accumulation in the population of algae (typically microscopic) in an aquatic system. Some blooms may be recognized by discoloration of the water resulting from the high density of pigmented cells. Visibility can severely deteriorate over a period of hours to days.</dd>

<span class="anchor" id="aLP"></span>
<dt class="glossary" id="alp" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">ALP</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Articulated_Loading_Platform&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Articulated Loading Platform (page does not exist)">Articulated Loading Platform</a>, a type of <a href="/wiki/Single_buoy_mooring" title="Single buoy mooring">single buoy mooring</a> consisting of a buoyant upper structure with a lattice leg linked by an articulating joint to a mooring.<sup id="cite_ref-HSE_terminology_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HSE_terminology-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="alternative_air_source" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">alternative air source</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Alternative_air_source" title="Alternative air source">Alternative air source</a></span></p>
A secondary supply of air or other breathing gas used by a diver in an emergency. See also <span title="See entry on this page at § emergency gas supply" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#emergency_gas_supply" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G">emergency gas supply</a></span> (EGS)</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="alternobaric_vertigo" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">alternobaric vertigo</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Alternobaric_vertigo" title="Alternobaric vertigo">Alternobaric vertigo</a></span></p>
Dizziness caused by different internal pressure in the middle ears.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="altitude_diving" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">altitude diving</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Altitude_diving" title="Altitude diving">Altitude diving</a></span></p>
Diving at a location where the water surface is at an altitude which requires modification of decompression schedules.<sup id="cite_ref-USNDM_R6_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USNDM_R6-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> (more than about 300&#160;m (980&#160;ft) above sea level.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="ambient_pressure" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">ambient pressure</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ambient_pressure" title="Ambient pressure">Ambient pressure</a></span></p>
Pressure of the local surroundings.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="anoxia" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">anoxia</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hypoxia_(medical)" title="Hypoxia (medical)">Hypoxia (medical)</a></span></p>
Tissues completely lacking in <a href="/wiki/Oxygen" title="Oxygen">oxygen</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="anoxic" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">anoxic</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Environment or gas completely lacking in oxygen.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="aodc" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">AODC</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Association_of_Offshore_Diving_Contractors&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Association of Offshore Diving Contractors (page does not exist)">Association of Offshore Diving Contractors</a>, one of the predecessors to the <a href="/wiki/International_Marine_Contractors_Association" title="International Marine Contractors Association">International Marine Contractors Association</a> (IMCA).<sup id="cite_ref-Gibson_OGP_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gibson_OGP-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="aphasia" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">aphasia</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Aphasia" title="Aphasia">Aphasia</a></span></p>
An impairment of language ability which may range from having difficulty remembering words to being completely unable to speak, read, or write</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="apnea" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">apnea</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;<a href="/wiki/Apnea" title="Apnea">Suspension of breathing</a>, breath-hold.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;<a href="/wiki/Freediving" title="Freediving">Freediving</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="appropriate_breathing_mix" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">appropriate breathing mix</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="appropriate_breathing_gas" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">appropriate breathing gas</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Scuba_gas_planning#Choosing_a_suitable_breathing_gas_mixture" title="Scuba gas planning">Scuba gas planning#Choosing a suitable breathing gas mixture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saturation_diving#Atmosphere_control" title="Saturation diving">Saturation diving#Atmosphere control</a></span></p>
A breathing gas mixture that is suitable in composition and temperature, and of adequate pressure, having regard to the system and equipment used in the diving operations, the work undertaken in those operations, and the conditions and depth at which they are to be carried out.<sup id="cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="aqua-lung" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Aqua-lung</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Aqua-lung" class="mw-redirect" title="Aqua-lung">Aqua-lung</a></span></p>
Self contained open circuit demand underwater breathing equipment consisting of a <a href="/wiki/Diving_cylinder" title="Diving cylinder">diving cylinder</a> and <a href="/wiki/Diving_regulator" title="Diving regulator">diving regulator</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="arterial_bubble_model" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">arterial bubble model</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/History_of_decompression_research_and_development#The_arterial_bubble_decompression_model" title="History of decompression research and development">History of decompression research and development#The arterial bubble decompression model</a></span></p>
Decompression model in which the filtering capacity of the lung is assumed to have a threshold radius of the size of a red blood cell and sufficiently small decompression bubbles can pass to the arterial side, especially during the initial phase of ascent.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="arterial_gas_embolism" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">arterial gas embolism</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Arterial_gas_embolism" class="mw-redirect" title="Arterial gas embolism">Arterial gas embolism</a></span></p>
Blockage of an artery by a gas bubble. A possible consequence of <a href="/wiki/Lung_overpressure_injury" class="mw-redirect" title="Lung overpressure injury">lung overpressure injury</a> and <a href="/wiki/Decompression_sickness" title="Decompression sickness">decompression sickness</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="articulated_loading_platform" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">articulated loading platform</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#aLP"><span title="See entry on this page at § ALP" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">ALP</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="ar_vest" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">AR vest</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A waistcoat (vest) style <a href="/wiki/Surface-supplied_diving#Jacket_harness" title="Surface-supplied diving">harness</a> of heavy cloth with strong adjustable webbing straps so that the diver can not slide out under any reasonably foreseeable circumstance.<sup id="cite_ref-ARvest_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ARvest-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="ascent" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">ascent</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Ascending_and_descending_(diving)" title="Ascending and descending (diving)">Ascending and descending (diving)</a></span></p>
Part of the dive profile where the diver is moving upwards towards the surface. An ascent may be interrupted by <span title="See entry on this page at § stops" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#stops" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S">stops</a></span> (q.v.), when the diver maintains a functionally constant depth for the purpose of decompression, and <span title="See entry on this page at § pulls" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#pulls" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S">pulls</a></span> (q.v.), during which periods there is consistently upwards movement (minor variations in the scale of a few seconds are generally ignored).</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="ascent_rate" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">ascent rate</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Decompression_practice#Ascent_rate" title="Decompression practice">Decompression practice#Ascent rate</a></span></p>
The rate at which depth is reduced at the end of a dive. An important component of decompression.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="a.s.s.e.t." style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">A.S.S.E.T.</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Association_of_SCUBA_Service_Engineers_and_Technicians&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Association of SCUBA Service Engineers and Technicians (page does not exist)">Association of SCUBA Service Engineers and Technicians</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Scuba_engineer_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scuba_engineer-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<span class="anchor" id="association_of_Diving_Contractors_International"></span>
<dt class="glossary" id="association_of_diving_contractors_international" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Association of Diving Contractors International</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also:"ADCI"</span></p>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/w/index.php?title=Association_of_Diving_Contractors_International&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Association of Diving Contractors International (page does not exist)">Association of Diving Contractors International</a></span></p> 
A non-profit organization to promote commercial diving, and establish and encourage observance of safe standards for commercial diving.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="ata" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">ATA</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="ata" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">ata</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="atmospheres_absolute" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">atmospheres absolute</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Standard_atmosphere_(unit)" title="Standard atmosphere (unit)">Standard atmosphere (unit)</a></span></p>
<a href="/wiki/Units_of_measurement" class="mw-redirect" title="Units of measurement">Unit</a> of <a href="/wiki/Absolute_pressure" class="mw-redirect" title="Absolute pressure">absolute pressure</a> equivalent to standard <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_pressure" title="Atmospheric pressure">atmospheric pressure</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="atmospheric_diving_suit" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">atmospheric diving suit</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="ads" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">ADS</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_diving_suit" title="Atmospheric diving suit">Atmospheric diving suit</a></span></p>
A small one-man articulated submersible of anthropomorphic form which resembles a suit of armour, with elaborate pressure joints to allow articulation while maintaining an internal pressure of one atmosphere.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="attack_swimmer" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">attack swimmer</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#combat_swimmer"><span title="See entry on this page at § combat swimmer" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">combat swimmer</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="attendant" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">attendant</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <span title="See entry on this page at § diver&#39;s attendant" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#diver&#39;s_attendant" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G">diver's attendant</a></span></span></p></dd>
<p><span class="anchor" id="australian_Diver_Accreditation_Scheme"></span>
</p>
<dt class="glossary" id="australian_diver_accreditation_scheme" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Australian Diver Accreditation Scheme</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Australian_Diver_Accreditation_Scheme" title="Australian Diver Accreditation Scheme">Australian Diver Accreditation Scheme</a></span></p> 
An international commercial and occupational diver certification scheme based in Australia.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="auto-closure_device" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">auto-closure device</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="automatic_closure_device" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">automatic closure device</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "ACD"</span></p> 
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Diving_regulator#Automatic_closure_device" title="Diving regulator">Diving regulator#Automatic closure device</a></span></p>
A mechanism for automatically closing off the inlet opening of a regulator first stage when it is disconnected from a cylinder to seal it against ingress of contamination.<sup id="cite_ref-ACD_Series_Yoke_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ACD_Series_Yoke-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Buzzacott_2018_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Buzzacott_2018-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="automatic_diluent_valve" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">automatic diluent valve</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Diving_regulator#Automatic_diluent_valve_(ADV)" title="Diving regulator">Automatic Diluent Valve</a></span></p>
A demand valve set into the breathing loop of a rebreather to inject <a href="/wiki/Diluent_gas" class="mw-redirect" title="Diluent gas">diluent gas</a> into the loop when the loop volume falls and there is not enough gas for inhalation.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="automatic_dump_valve" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">automatic dump valve</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Adjustable spring-loaded overpressure valve with manual override used on a <a href="#constant_volume_dry_suit"><span title="See entry on this page at § constant volume dry suit" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">constant volume dry suit</span></a> to automatically discharge excess suit inflation gas as it expands during ascent, thereby maintaining a nearly constant volume and buoyancy of the suit.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="autonomous_diver" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Autonomous diver</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_diver" title="Autonomous diver">Autonomous diver</a></span></p> 
EN 14153-2 / ISO 24801-2 standard competence for recreational scuba diver. The level 2 "Autonomous diver" has sufficient knowledge, skill and experience to make dives, in open water, which do not require in-water decompression stops, to a recommended maximum depth of 20&#160;m with other scuba divers of the same level, only when appropriate support is available at the surface, and under conditions that are equal or better than the conditions in which they were trained, without supervision of a scuba instructor, unless they have additional training or are accompanied by a <a href="/wiki/Dive_leader" title="Dive leader">dive leader</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-EUF_certification_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EUF_certification-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="available_gas" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">available gas</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Scuba_gas_planning#Available_gas" title="Scuba gas planning">Scuba gas planning#Available gas</a></span></p> 
Breathing gas available from a cylinder after taking into account ambient pressure and the pressure needed for correct function of the delivery system at a useful flow rate. This may also take into account a reserve allocation.</dd> 
 
</dl>
