<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Decompression_theory#Thermodynamic_model_and_deep_stops" title="Decompression theory">Decompression theory#Thermodynamic model and deep stops</a></span></p>
Decompression stops which are deeper than the deepest stops required by decompression algorithms using dissolved phase models.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="deep_water_blackout" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">deep water blackout</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;Freediving: An ambiguous alternative term for <a href="/wiki/Freediving_blackout#Ascent_blackout" title="Freediving blackout">blackout of ascent</a> following a deep breath-hold dive, in which loss of consciousness occurs as the surface is approached, or at the surface, caused by cerebral hypoxia arising from the rapid drop in the partial pressure of oxygen in the lungs during ascent as the ambient pressure drops and the gas in the lungs expands to surface volume.<sup id="cite_ref-Lindholm_2006_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lindholm_2006-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup></dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;Scuba and surface-supplied diving: Loss of consciousness in <a href="/wiki/Deep_diving#Ultra_deep_air" title="Deep diving">deep air diving</a> at depths below 50&#160;m with no clear primary cause, associated with <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen_narcosis" title="Nitrogen narcosis">nitrogen narcosis</a>, a neurological impairment with anaesthetic effects caused by high partial pressure of nitrogen dissolved in nerve tissue, and possibly acute <a href="/wiki/Oxygen_toxicity" title="Oxygen toxicity">oxygen toxicity</a>. The term is not in widespread use at present.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="dehydration" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">dehydration</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Dehydration" title="Dehydration">Dehydration</a></span></p>
A condition where the water content of the body is reduced.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="delta_p" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">delta P</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="δp" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">ΔP</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="δp" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">δp</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Environments where a pressure difference causes flow. Usually refers to cases where the flow is likely to entrain and pull the diver into an enclosed space or through an opening.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="demand_helmet" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">demand helmet</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See; <a href="/wiki/Surface-supplied_diving#Lightweight_demand_helmets" title="Surface-supplied diving">Surface-supplied diving#Lightweight demand helmets</a></span></p>
Diving helmet which provides breathing gas supply flow only when the diver inhales, triggered by the pressure drop.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="demand_valve" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">demand valve</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Diving_regulator#Demand_valve" title="Diving regulator">Diving regulator#Demand valve</a></span></p>
Mechanism for providing the user with breathing gas flow only when required. The valve may be triggered by a reduction of pressure across the actuator diaphragm to below ambient due to inhalation, or by pressing a manual override (Purge button).</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="depth_gauge" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">depth gauge</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Depth_gauge" title="Depth gauge">Depth gauge</a></span></p>
A pressure gauge calibrated to measure depth as a function of ambient pressure.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="descending_line" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">descending line</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See also: <span title="See entry on this page at § jackstay" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O#jackstay" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: H–O">jackstay</a></span>, <a href="#downline"><span title="See entry on this page at § downline" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">downline</span></a> and <span title="See entry on this page at § shotline" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#shotline" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S">shotline</a></span></span></p>
A substantial heavily weighted line attached to a secure point at the surface, such as a boat or buoy, which can be used by a diver to control position and depth during descent an ascent.<sup id="cite_ref-USN_training_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USN_training-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="developed_pressure" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">developed pressure</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Diving_cylinder#Developed_pressure" title="Diving cylinder">Diving cylinder#Developed pressure</a></span></p>
The pressure of the compressed gas in a cylinder at a temperature other than the nominal temperature at which charging pressure is specified. Usually refers to pressure when fully charged at a variation from the reference temperature.<sup id="cite_ref-SANS_10019_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SANS_10019-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="dgps" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">DGPS</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Differential_Global_Positioning_System" class="mw-redirect" title="Differential Global Positioning System">Differential Global Positioning System</a></span></p>
An enhancement to Global Positioning System that provides improved location accuracy. DGPS uses a network of fixed, ground-based reference stations to broadcast the difference between the positions indicated by the satellite systems and the known fixed positions.</dd>
</dl>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Di">Di</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Di">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt class="glossary" id="diamond_reef_system" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Diamond Reef System</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Diamond_Reef_System" title="Diamond Reef System">Diamond Reef System</a></span></p>
A diving skills program that uses a set of standardized portable obstacles to train and evaluate buoyancy skills and educate scuba divers on how to interact with coral reefs.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="differential_pressure_hazard" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">differential pressure hazard</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="delta_p_hazard" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">delta P hazard</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Situation where water flows from a region of higher pressure to one of lower pressure, and where obstructing the flow will induce a large force on the obstruction. A type of diving hazard.<sup id="cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="diffusion_limited" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">diffusion limited</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Decompression_theory#Diffusion_limited_tissues_and_the_&quot;Tissue_slab&quot;,_and_series_models" title="Decompression theory">Decompression theory#Diffusion limited tissues and the "Tissue slab", and series models</a></span></p>
Decompression hypothesis that the uptake and elimination of inert gas is limited by diffusion rates in the tissues. Compare with <span title="See entry on this page at § perfusion limited" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#perfusion_limited" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S">perfusion limited</a></span>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="diluent" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">diluent</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "dil"</span></p>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See <a href="/wiki/Rebreather#Gas_sources" title="Rebreather">Rebreather#Gas sources</a></span></p>
Gas mixture used to dilute the oxygen in the loop of a closed circuit rebreather to a partial pressure suited to the depth.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="diluent_flush" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">diluent flush</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "flush", "dil flush", "loop flush"</span></p>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See <a href="/wiki/Rebreather_diving#Diluent_flush" title="Rebreather diving">Rebreather diving#Diluent flush</a></span></p> 
Replacing the gas within the breathing loop of a rebreather by injecting diluent gas while venting the previous gas mix. Usually done to get a breathable mixture of known composition in the loop to check calibration of the oxygen cells.<sup id="cite_ref-Heinerth_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heinerth-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="din_fitting" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">DIN fitting</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "DIN valve", "DIN regulator", "DIN thread"</span></p>
Usually refers to G5/8" x 14 tpi<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> parallel <a href="/wiki/Screw_thread" title="Screw thread">thread</a> fittings used to connect a <a href="/wiki/Diving_cylinder#Connection_to_the_regulator" title="Diving cylinder">cylinder valve</a> to a filling connection or <a href="/wiki/Diving_regulator#First_stage" title="Diving regulator">regulator first stage</a>. Available in 200 bar and 300 bar versions which should only be inter-connectable in safe combinations. 232 bar DIN (5-thread, G5/8) Outlet/Connector #13 to DIN 477 part 1, and 300 bar DIN (7-thread, G5/8) Outlet/Connector #56 to DIN 477 part 5 - these are similar to 5-thread DIN fitting but are rated to 300 bar working pressures. The 300 bar pressures are common in European diving and in US cave diving.<sup id="cite_ref-Scuba_Doctor_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scuba_Doctor-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="din_plug" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">DIN plug</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Diving_cylinder#Connection_to_the_regulator" title="Diving cylinder">Diving cylinder#Connection to the regulator</a></span></p>
Screw in adaptor which can be used with many recent 200/240 bar <a href="/wiki/Deutsches_Institut_f%C3%BCr_Normung" title="Deutsches Institut für Normung">DIN</a> cylinder valves to allow connection of Yoke regulators or filling whips.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="dir" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">DIR</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#doing_It_Right"><span title="See entry on this page at § Doing It Right" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">Doing It Right</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="direct_ascent" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">direct ascent</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Uninterrupted vertical ascent to the water's surface without decompression stops, usually also without a safety stop</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="display_integrated_vibratory_alarm" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">display integrated vibratory alarm</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "DIVA"</span></p>
Display integrated vibrating alarm – A <span title="See entry on this page at § head-up display" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O#head-up_display" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: H–O">head-up display</a></span> module which produces a warning vibration to draw the attention of the diver, generally mounted on the diver's mask or the rebreather mouthpiece.<sup id="cite_ref-Heinerth_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heinerth-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="distance_line" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">distance line</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "penetration line" or "guideline"</span></p>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article <a href="/wiki/Distance_line" title="Distance line">Distance line</a></span></p>
A line used by scuba divers as a means of returning to a safe starting point in conditions of low visibility, water currents or where pilotage is difficult.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="diva" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">DIVA</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#display_integrated_vibratory_alarm"><span title="See entry on this page at § display integrated vibratory alarm" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">display integrated vibratory alarm</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="dive" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">dive</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">(legal) A human activity in which a person enters water or any other liquid, or a chamber in which they are subject to a pressure greater than 100 millibars above atmospheric pressure and, while in such an environment, they breathe air or other gas at a pressure greater than atmospheric pressure.<sup id="cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DR_2009_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DR_2009-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="dive_computer" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">dive computer</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "decompression computer"</span></p>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Dive_computer" title="Dive computer">Dive computer</a></span></p>
A device used by a <a href="/wiki/Scuba_diving" title="Scuba diving">scuba diver</a> to measure the time and depth of a dive so that a safe ascent profile can be calculated and displayed so that the diver can avoid <a href="/wiki/Decompression_sickness" title="Decompression sickness">decompression sickness</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-aaus_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aaus-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="dive_factor" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">dive factor</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Factor used in gas consumption estimates which allows for increased breathing rate due to conditions other than depth. Values range from 1.1 for relaxed, stress free conditions to more than 3.0 for heavy work.<sup id="cite_ref-SDI_Solo_IG_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SDI_Solo_IG-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="dive_flag" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">dive flag</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Flag used to indicate that there are divers in the water. There are two versions: the <a href="/wiki/International_maritime_signal_flags" title="International maritime signal flags">international code letter flag 'Alpha'</a>, <a href="/wiki/File:ICS_Alpha.svg" class="image"><img alt="ICS Alpha.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/ICS_Alpha.svg/15px-ICS_Alpha.svg.png" decoding="async" width="15" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/ICS_Alpha.svg/23px-ICS_Alpha.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/ICS_Alpha.svg/30px-ICS_Alpha.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600" /></a>, and the red flag with white diagonal bar, <a href="/wiki/File:ICS_Diver.svg" class="image"><img alt="ICS Diver.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/ICS_Diver.svg/15px-ICS_Diver.svg.png" decoding="async" width="15" height="15" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/ICS_Diver.svg/23px-ICS_Diver.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/ICS_Diver.svg/30px-ICS_Diver.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600" /></a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="dive_ladder" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">dive ladder</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="diver_ladder" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">diver ladder</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Human_factors_in_diving_equipment_design#Diver_ladders" title="Human factors in diving equipment design">Human factors in diving equipment design#Diver ladders</a></span></p>
A ladder suitable for divers dressed for the specific dive to climb up and down between the surface deployment area and the water.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="dive_leader" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Dive Leader</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">EN 14153-3 / ISO 24801-3 standard competence for recreational scuba diver. A level 3 "Dive Leader" has sufficient knowledge, skill and experience to plan, organise and conduct their dives and lead other recreational scuba divers in open water, to conduct any specialised recreational scuba diving activities for which they have received appropriate training, plan and execute emergency procedures appropriate for the diving environment and activities. If diving and environmental conditions are significantly different from those previously experienced, they require an appropriate orientation with regard to local environmental conditions, and must have appropriate specialised training and experience to lead on dives which have more demanding operational parameters.<sup id="cite_ref-EUF_level_3_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EUF_level_3-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="dive_location" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">dive location</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">(Professional) The vessel, structure, or base from which occupational dives are conducted and supported. More specifically, the point from which the actual dive is controlled.<sup id="cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="dive_marshall" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">dive marshall</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Recreational and club diving equivalent of a diving supervisor. The person who organizes and plans a group dive outing for recreational divers, assesses risk, logs divers into and out of the water and is available at the site to manage incident response.<sup id="cite_ref-Crabbsac_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Crabbsac-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="divemaster" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">divemaster</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Divemaster" title="Divemaster">Divemaster</a></span></p>
A professional level recreational diver who leads a group of less experienced or visiting divers underwater.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="dive_platform" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">dive platform</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;Recreational: Fixed or movable platform on a <a href="/wiki/Dive_boat" title="Dive boat">dive boat</a> which divers use to more easily enter and leave the water.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;Commercial: Structure on which the <a href="#diving_spread"><span title="See entry on this page at § diving spread" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">diving spread</span></a> is established. Usually a vessel or an offshore or waterside structure.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="dive_profile" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">dive profile</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Dive_profile" title="Dive profile">Dive profile</a></span></p>
The variation of depth with elapsed time during a dive, often depicted as a graph.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="dive_site" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">dive site</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Dive_site" class="mw-redirect" title="Dive site">Dive site</a></span></p>
The place at which the dive occurs. Also, more broadly, a place at which diving occurs, has occurred, or is planned to occur, and the general locality, with extent depending on context. Professional divers may also refer to a work site, or search area if relevant.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="dive_skins" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">dive skins</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A <a href="/wiki/Lycra" class="mw-redirect" title="Lycra">lycra</a> suit worn by a diver in warm water or under a wet suit.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="dive_station" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">dive station</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The site from which a professional diving operation is directly controlled.<sup id="cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_8-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="dive_tables" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">dive tables</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#decompression_tables"><span title="See entry on this page at § decompression tables" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">decompression tables</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="dive_time" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">dive time</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The total elapsed time spent underwater during a dive.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="dive_timer" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">dive timer</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Dive_timer" class="mw-redirect" title="Dive timer">Dive timer</a></span></p>
An automatically operated electronic timer which records the elapsed time from the start of a dive.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="diver_lift" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">diver lift</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Dive_boat#Diver_lifts" title="Dive boat">Dive boat#Diver lifts</a></span></p>
A mechanism used to lower one or more divers into the water to a shallow depth, and to lift them out again.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="diver_training_manual" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">diver training manual</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See also: <a href="/wiki/Training_manual" title="Training manual">Training manual</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Diving_manual&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Diving manual (page does not exist)">Diving manual</a></span></p>
A publication containing instructional material for diver training. This may relate to a specific certification or a range of certifications, and is usually published either by a certification agency or a diving school for their own use, but may also be published and sold for general consumption.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="diver_transfer_chamber" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">diver transfer chamber</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Hyperbaric chamber connecting other component chambers of a saturation life support system which may be at different pressures.<sup id="cite_ref-USNDM_R6_3-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USNDM_R6-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="diver_umbilical" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">diver umbilical</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="diver&#39;s_umbilical" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">diver's umbilical</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Umbilical_cable#Diver" title="Umbilical cable">Umbilical cable#Diver</a></span></p> 
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See also: <span title="See entry on this page at § umbilical cable" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z#umbilical_cable" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: T–Z">umbilical cable</a></span></span></p> 
Bundle of life-support hoses, communication cable, pneumofathomer hose and strength member between the surface control point and a surface-supplied diver.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="divers_alert_network" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Divers Alert Network</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "DAN"</span></p>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article <a href="/wiki/Divers_Alert_Network" title="Divers Alert Network">Divers Alert Network</a></span></p>
A non-profit organization for assisting divers in medical and travel emergencies, advising divers on medical matters, and medical research on recreational diving safety.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="diver&#39;s_attendant" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">diver's attendant</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "dive tender" and "line attendant"<sup id="cite_ref-DR_2001_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DR_2001-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup></span></p>
A person who assists the working diver to prepare for a dive, get in and out of the water, and to undress from the diving equipment, and who tends the lifeline or umbilical while the diver is in the water.<sup id="cite_ref-DR_2001_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DR_2001-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="diver&#39;s_slate" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">diver's slate</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: wrist slate</span></p>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See also: <span title="See entry on this page at § wet notes" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z#wet_notes" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: T–Z">wet notes</a></span></span></p>
Piece of opaque white or pale coloured rigid plastic sheet with matte finish that is easily marked with a graphite pencil, used for taking notes, making sketches and written communication underwater.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="dive/surface_valve" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">dive/surface valve</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Rebreather#Dive/Surface_valve" title="Rebreather">Rebreather#Dive/Surface valve</a></span></p> 
Valve on the mouthpiece of a rebreather which can be switched between the loop and ambient air at the surface. It seals the breathing loop on the surface setting to prevent flooding the loop and is used for this purpose if the mouthpiece is removed from the mouth in the water. Compare with <span title="See entry on this page at § bailout valve" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#bailout_valve" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C">bailout valve</a></span> (BOV).</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="diving" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">diving</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Underwater activity and related recompression facility operations where personnel are subjected to elevated ambient pressure.<sup id="cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_8-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="diving_basket" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">diving basket</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A diver deployment device similar to a <a href="#diving_stage"><span title="See entry on this page at § diving stage" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">diving stage</span></a>, normally designed with an open cage.<sup id="cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_8-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="diving_bell" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">diving bell</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Diving_bell" title="Diving bell">Diving bell</a></span></p>
A rigid chamber suspended from a cable and used to transport divers to depth and back to the surface.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="diving_chamber" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">diving chamber</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;A simple form of submersible vessel to take divers underwater and to provide a temporary base and retrieval system in the depths (<a href="/wiki/Diving_bell" title="Diving bell">diving bell</a>).</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;A land or ship-based <a href="/wiki/Diving_chamber" title="Diving chamber">hyperbaric chamber</a> to artificially reproduce the hyperbaric conditions under the sea.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="diving_contractor" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">diving contractor</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Legal persona responsible for commercial diving operations.<sup id="cite_ref-DR_2009_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DR_2009-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="diving_depth" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">diving depth</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Generally the maximum depth to which the diver is exposed during a dive.<sup id="cite_ref-EDTC_2017_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EDTC_2017-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="diving_heavy" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">diving heavy</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See also: <span title="See entry on this page at § overweighting" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O#overweighting" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: H–O">overweighting</a></span></span></p>
Practice of carrying significantly more ballast weight than necessary to neutralise buoyancy. Common in professional diving operations where the diver needs to remain in firm contact with the bottom to work effectively, and is tethered by a lifeline or umbilical to a control point at a place of safety, which is managed by a tender.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="diving_manual" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">diving manual</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;<i>See: <span title="See entry on this page at § operations manual" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O#operations_manual" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: H–O">operations manual</a></span></i></dd> 
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;<i>See: <a href="#diver_training_manual"><span title="See entry on this page at § diver training manual" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">diver training manual</span></a></i></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="diving_medical_advisory_council" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Diving Medical Advisory Council</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "DMAC"</span></p>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article <a href="/wiki/Diving_Medical_Advisory_Council" title="Diving Medical Advisory Council">Diving Medical Advisory Council</a></span></p> 
An independent body of diving medical specialists from Northern Europe which provides advice about medical and certain safety aspects of commercial diving.<sup id="cite_ref-DMAC_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DMAC-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="diving_medical_technician" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">diving medical technician</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "DMT"</span></p>
A <a href="/wiki/Paramedic" title="Paramedic">paramedic</a> specialising in diving related conditions, and medically fit to dive in a hyperbaric chamber.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="diving_method" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">diving method</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="diving_mode" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">diving mode</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Diving_mode" class="mw-redirect" title="Diving mode">Diving mode</a></span></p>
The combination of diving equipment, breathing medium and compression/decompression used for a diving operation, e.g. breathhold, open circuit scuba, nitrox rebreather, surface-supplied air, heliox saturation, etc.<sup id="cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_8-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="diving_operation" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">diving operation</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Diving_operation" class="mw-redirect" title="Diving operation">Diving operation</a></span></p>
A portion of a diving project that can be safely supervised by one person, which can be a single dive or a number of dives.<sup id="cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_8-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="diving_procedure" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">diving procedure</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Sequence of actions used to achieve a specific outcome during a diving operation. Often standardised, and based on experience of the procedure being safe and efficient. May be specified, recommended, or authorised by a training manual, <a href="/wiki/Operations_manual" title="Operations manual">operations manual</a> or <a href="/wiki/Code_of_practice" title="Code of practice">code of practice</a>, and may have to be adapted to suit circumstances, while remaining essentially similar. See <a href="/wiki/Standard_operating_procedure" title="Standard operating procedure">Standard operating procedure</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="diving_project" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">diving project</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The overall diving job by a <a href="/wiki/Diving_contractor" class="mw-redirect" title="Diving contractor">diving contractor</a> under a specific contract or plan, regardless of duration.<sup id="cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_8-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DR_2009_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DR_2009-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="diving_regulator" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">diving regulator</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <span title="See entry on this page at § regulator" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#regulator" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S">regulator</a></span></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="diving_response" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">diving response</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="diving_reflex" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">diving reflex</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Diving_reflex" title="Diving reflex">Diving reflex</a></span></p>
The involuntary physiological response to immersion which exists in all air-breathing vertebrates. It is a series of autonomic responses to apnea which are strengthened by facial cooling and hypoxia. It consists of peripheral vasoconstriction and associated hypertension, vagally induced bradycardia and reduction of cardiac output. This appears to preferentially supply oxygen to the brain. Another aspect is splenic contraction which increases haemoglobin content of the blood.<sup id="cite_ref-Lindholm_and_Lundgren_2009_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lindholm_and_Lundgren_2009-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="diving_safety_officer" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">diving safety officer</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Diving_safety_officer" title="Diving safety officer">Diving safety officer</a></span></p>
The person who administers a United States university's research diving safety program.<sup id="cite_ref-sio2003_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sio2003-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="diving_signals" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">diving signals</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Diver_communications" title="Diver communications">Diver communications</a></span></p>
Hand sign and light sign system used by scuba divers to communicate when underwater.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="diving_stage" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">diving stage</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "basket"</span></p>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Decompression_practice#Diving_stages_and_wet_bells" title="Decompression practice">Decompression practice#Diving stages and wet bells</a></span></p>
A platform on which a diver stands which is hoisted into the water, lowered to the workplace at the bottom, and then hoisted up again to return the diver to the surface and lift them out of the water. The diving stage is particularly effective for controlling rate of descent and ascent.<sup id="cite_ref-DR_2001_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DR_2001-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="diving_superintendent" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">diving superintendent</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Person with overall responsibility for commercial diving operations at a large installation.<sup id="cite_ref-Bevan_2005_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bevan_2005-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="diving_supervisor" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">diving supervisor</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Diving_supervisor" title="Diving supervisor">Diving supervisor</a></span></p>
Person in charge of, and responsible for safety of a commercial diving operation. Usually trained, assessed as competent, certified and registered. Formally appointed by the diving contractor.<sup id="cite_ref-EDTC_2017_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EDTC_2017-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="diving_support_vessel" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">diving support vessel</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "DSV"</span></p> 
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Diving_support_vessel" title="Diving support vessel">Diving support vessel</a></span></p> 
A ship or boat used as a base for diving operations, particularly if designed or fitted out for that purpose.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="diving_system" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">diving system</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The complete set of equipment necessary to support a diving operation.<sup id="cite_ref-EDTC_2017_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EDTC_2017-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> The equipment and facilities required to execute the planned diving activity, including compression, decompression, rescue and recovery.<sup id="cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_8-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="dmac" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">DMAC</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <span title="See entry on this page at § Diving Medical Advisory Council" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G#Diving_Medical_Advisory_Council" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: D–G">Diving Medical Advisory Council</a></span></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="dmt" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">DMT</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#diving_medical_technician"><span title="See entry on this page at § Diving medical technician" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">Diving medical technician</span></a></span></p></dd>
</dl>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Do">Do</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Do">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt class="glossary" id="doing_it_right" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Doing It Right</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "DIR"</span></p>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Doing_It_Right_(scuba_diving)" title="Doing It Right (scuba diving)">Doing It Right</a></span></p>
A holistic approach to scuba diving, which encompasses several essential elements, including fundamental diving skills, teamwork, physical fitness, strictly defined standard procedures, and the use of standardised, streamlined and minimalistic equipment configurations.<sup id="cite_ref-Wrolf_Courtney_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wrolf_Courtney-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="dome_port" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">dome port</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A domed window of optical quality glass or plastic which covers the front of an underwater camera or video housing.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="donating_the_octopus" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">donating the octopus</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#donating_the_secondary"><span title="See entry on this page at § donating the secondary" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">donating the secondary</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="donating_the_primary" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">donating the primary</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Rescue technique where the donor of breathing gas provides it via the primary second stage – the one from which the donor was breathing – as it is known to be working and providing the correct gas. The donor then switches to their backup DV, often stowed under the chin by a bungee necklace with a breakaway connection.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="donating_the_secondary" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">donating the secondary</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Rescue technique where the donor of breathing gas provides it via the secondary, or octopus, second stage, and continues to breathe off the primary.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="donkey_dick" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">donkey dick</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Slang term for the corrugated buoyancy compensator inflation and deflation hose.<sup id="cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="doppler_bubble_detection" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Doppler bubble detection</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Decompression_theory#Doppler_ultrasonic_bubble_detection" title="Decompression theory">Decompression theory#Doppler ultrasonic bubble detection</a></span></p>
Ultrasonic signals reflected from bubble surfaces to identify and quantify gas bubbles present in venous blood.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="dorf_arrow" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Dorf arrow</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "line arrow"</span></p>
Triangular plastic line marker with two slots which is mounted on a cave guide line to indicate the direction of the exit.<sup id="cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_1-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="downline" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">downline</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="down_line" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">down line</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A rope leading from the surface down to the underwater workplace which allows a commercial diver to travel directly to and from the job site and to control rate of descent and ascent in the same way as using a shotline. Also sometimes called a jackstay.<sup id="cite_ref-Barsky_and_Christensen_2004_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Barsky_and_Christensen_2004-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> A downline used for open ocean diving is much the same as a shotline (q.v.), but does not reach all the way to the bottom. An open-ocean downline is weighted at the bottom, and attached to a substantial float at the surface, which may be tethered to the boat. It may be marked at intervals by knots or loops, and may be attached to decompression trapeze system. In some cases a sea anchor may be used to limit wind drift, particularly if attached to a boat with significant windage.<sup id="cite_ref-NOAA_12.6_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA_12.6-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="downstream" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">downstream</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">In the direction of flow. Displaced from the reference point in the direction of flow</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="downstream_valve" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">downstream valve</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Diving_regulator#Upstream_vs_downstream" title="Diving regulator">Diving regulator#Upstream vs downstream</a></span></p>
Valve in which the closure is downstream of the orifice. Pressure in the line tends to assist in opening the valve. When spring-loaded a downstream valve may open automatically if the pressure difference is excessive, thus functioning as a pressure relief valve</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="down_time" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">down time</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Period when planned activities can not be done due to unforeseen or uncontrollable circumstances.<sup id="cite_ref-Bevan_2005_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bevan_2005-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="dp_alert" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">DP alert</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Status of the <a href="/wiki/Dynamic_positioning" title="Dynamic positioning">dynamic positioning</a> system regarding positional accuracy and reliability. Green indicates normal operation, yellow indicates degraded operation and red indicates emergency.<sup id="cite_ref-Bevan_2005_21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bevan_2005-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="dp_footprint" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">DP footprint</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Dynamic_positioning" title="Dynamic positioning">Dynamic positioning</a> footprint: The area around the nominal position to which a dynamically positioned vessel is constrained by the DP system.<sup id="cite_ref-Bevan_2005_21-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bevan_2005-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="dpv" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">DPV</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;See: <a href="#diver_propulsion_vehicle"><span title="See entry on this page at § diver propulsion vehicle" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">diver propulsion vehicle</span></a></dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;See: <a href="#dynamically_positioned_vessel"><span title="See entry on this page at § dynamically positioned vessel" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">dynamically positioned vessel</span></a></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="d-ring" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">D-ring</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A ring shaped like a capital D, usually of stainless steel or plastic, stitched or buckled to a diver's harness and used as an attachment point for lifeline, cylinders or other equipment.<sup id="cite_ref-Wrolf_Courtney_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wrolf_Courtney-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="dräger_tube" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Dräger tube</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="draeger_tube" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">Draeger tube</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Indicator tube used for testing breathing gas quality.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="drift_diving" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">drift diving</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Drift_diving" title="Drift diving">drift diving</a></span></p>
Any dive where the diver is transported significantly by drifting with currents during the dive.<sup id="cite_ref-Wrolf_Courtney_22-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wrolf_Courtney-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="drillship" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">drillship</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Ship built or converted for offshore well drilling, using dynamic positioning to maintain position in deep water.<sup id="cite_ref-Bevan_2005_21-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bevan_2005-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="drop_cylinder" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">drop cylinder</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <span title="See entry on this page at § stage cylinder" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#stage_cylinder" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S">stage cylinder</a></span></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="drop_weight" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">drop weight</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Weight used during descent and ascent, but left on the bottom at the guideline during the deep part of the dive when it is not needed due to suit compression.<sup id="cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_1-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="drowning" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">drowning</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Drowning" title="Drowning">Drowning</a></span></p>
The process of experiencing respiratory impairment from submersion/immersion in liquid.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="dry_bag" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">dry bag</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Dry_bag" title="Dry bag">Dry bag</a></span></p>
Bag which seals in a watertight manner. Used for keeping clothes and other equipment dry in a wet environment.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="dry_bell" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">dry bell</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <span title="See entry on this page at § closed bell" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#closed_bell" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C">closed bell</a></span></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="dry_filling" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">dry filling</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Diving_cylinder#Temperature_change_during_filling" title="Diving cylinder">Diving cylinder#Temperature change during filling</a></span></p>
Filling scuba cylinders without the use of a water bath for cooling.<sup id="cite_ref-Dry_filling_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dry_filling-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="dry_suit" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">dry suit</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Dry_suit" title="Dry suit">Dry suit</a></span></p>
A watertight suit worn to keep the diver dry and to provide protection from the environment. Thermal insulation may be provided by the suit or garments worn under the suit.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="dry_suit_blowup" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">dry suit blowup</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Dry_suit#Over-inflation" title="Dry suit">Dry suit#Over-inflation</a></span></p>
Uncontrolled ascent due to over-inflation of a dry suit.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="dsv" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">DSV</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;See: <a href="#dive/surface_valve"><span title="See entry on this page at § dive/surface valve" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">dive/surface valve</span></a></dd> 
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;See: <a href="#diving_support_vessel"><span title="See entry on this page at § diving support vessel" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">diving support vessel</span></a></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="dsmb" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">DSMB</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "delayed surface marker buoy" and "decompression buoy"</span></p>
An inflatable marker buoy deployed from underwater to indicate the position of a diver and to control ascent rate. Can also be used to mark a position or signal an emergency.</dd>
</dl>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Du">Du</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Du">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt class="glossary" id="duckbill_valve" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">duckbill valve</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Duckbill_valve" title="Duckbill valve">Duckbill valve</a></span></p>
A non-return valve, manufactured from rubber or synthetic elastomer, and shaped somewhat like the beak of a duck. Used as exhaust valve in some twin-hose diving regulators</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="dump_line" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">dump line</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A rope attached to the dump valve on a <a href="/wiki/Lift_bag" class="mw-redirect" title="Lift bag">lift bag</a> which is used by a diver to operate the dump valve to release air for control and adjustment of the bag buoyancy.<sup id="cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_8-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="dump_valve" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">dump valve</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Valve used to release excess gas from a dry suit, buoyancy compensator, rebreather, or lift bag. Usually manually operated in buoyancy compensators and lift bags, and <a href="#automatic_dump_valve"><span title="See entry on this page at § automatic dump valve" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">automatic</span></a> in dry suits and rebreathers. May also function as an <span title="See entry on this page at § overpressure valve" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O#overpressure_valve" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: H–O">overpressure valve</a></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_1-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="dwell_time" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">dwell time</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dwell_time_(filtration)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Dwell time (filtration) (page does not exist)">Dwell time (filtration)</a></span></p> 
Time that the breathing gas passing through a filter stack or absorbent canister remains in contact with the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Active_filtration&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Active filtration (page does not exist)">active filtration</a> medium where the absorption of impurities can occur.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="dynamically_positioned_vessel" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">dynamically positioned vessel</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Dynamic_positioning" title="Dynamic positioning">Dynamic positioning</a></span></p>
Vessel which maintains position and heading using thrusters and positional feedback <sup id="cite_ref-Wrolf_Courtney_22-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wrolf_Courtney-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="dynamic_positioning" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">dynamic positioning</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Dynamic_positioning" title="Dynamic positioning">Dynamic positioning</a></span></p>
Method of keeping a floating platform in position without anchoring, using thrusters and positional feedback.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="dynamic_setpoint" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">dynamic setpoint</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "floating setpoint"</span></p>
A target value for oxygen partial pressure in a rebreather loop which varies as a function of depth. Generally a setpoint that changes to optimize gas use, no stop time and other dive variables.<sup id="cite_ref-Heinerth_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heinerth-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="dysbarism" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">dysbarism</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Dysbarism" title="Dysbarism">Dysbarism</a></span></p>
Medical conditions resulting from changes in ambient pressure.</dd>

</dl>
