<p><a href="#References">References</a>
</p>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<dl class="glossary">

<dt class="glossary" id="ead" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">EAD</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See <a href="#equivalent_air_depth"><span title="See entry on this page at § equivalent air depth" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">equivalent air depth</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="ean" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">EAN</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See <a href="#enriched_Air_Nitrox"><span title="See entry on this page at § Enriched Air Nitrox" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">Enriched Air Nitrox</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="ear_beer" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">ear beer</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A home made mixture of alcohol and acetic acid in water used as a drying agent and disinfectant to rinse the ears after diving, to prevent ear infections.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="ear_clearing" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">ear clearing</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article <a href="/wiki/Ear_clearing" title="Ear clearing">Ear clearing</a></span></p>
Equalising the pressure in the middle and external ear by opening the Eustachian tubes. Several techniques are used.<sup id="cite_ref-NOAA_4th_ed_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA_4th_ed-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="eccr" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">ECCR</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="ecccr" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">ECCCR</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Diving_rebreather#Control_of_the_breathing_gas_mix" title="Diving rebreather">Diving rebreather#Control of the breathing gas mix</a></span></p>
Electronic closed circuit <a href="/wiki/Rebreather" title="Rebreather">rebreather</a>. Sometimes ECCCR for electronically controlled closed circuit rebreather, which is the same thing.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="eddy_current_test" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">eddy current test</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Eddy-current_testing" title="Eddy-current testing">Eddy-current testing</a></span></p>
Method of <a href="/wiki/Non-destructive_testing" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-destructive testing">non-destructive testing</a> using electromagnetic induction to detect flaws in conductive materials. It is used to detect cracks in parallel neck threads of aluminium cylinders. Also called <span title="See entry on this page at § Visual Plus inspection" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z#Visual_Plus_inspection" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: T–Z">Visual Plus inspection</a></span>. Required for cylinders of <span title="See entry on this page at § AA6351" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#AA6351" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C">AA6351</a></span> alloy.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="edtc" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">EDTC</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><a href="#european_Diving_Technology_Committee"><span title="See entry on this page at § European Diving Technology Committee" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">European Diving Technology Committee</span></a></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="egs" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">EGS</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#emergency_gas_supply"><span title="See entry on this page at § emergency gas supply" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">emergency gas supply</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="e-l_algorithm" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">E-L algorithm</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#vVAL18"><span title="See entry on this page at § VVAL18" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">VVAL18</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="electro-galvanic_oxygen_sensor" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">electro-galvanic oxygen sensor</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Electro-galvanic_oxygen_sensor" title="Electro-galvanic oxygen sensor">electro-galvanic oxygen sensor</a></span></p> 
An <a href="/wiki/Electro-chemical_fuel_cell" class="mw-redirect" title="Electro-chemical fuel cell">Electro-chemical fuel cell</a> which produces a voltage proportional to the partial pressure of oxygen.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="emergency_gas_supply" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">emergency gas supply</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See also: <span title="See entry on this page at § bailout cylinder" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#bailout_cylinder" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C">bailout cylinder</a></span></span></p>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bailout_bottle" title="Bailout bottle">Bailout bottle</a>,  also <a href="/wiki/Surface-supplied_diving#Bailout_gas_supply" title="Surface-supplied diving">Surface-supplied diving#Bailout gas supply</a></span></p>
Breathing gas supply to a diver that is intended for use in a failure of primary, and where applicable, secondary, breathing gas supply systems. More than one emergency gas supply may be available, of which at least one is usually carried by the diver (scuba).</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="emergency_position_indicating_radio_beacon" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">emergency position indicating radio beacon</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="emergency_position_indicating_radiobeacon" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">emergency position indicating radiobeacon</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "emergency beacon" or "EPIRB"</span></p>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Emergency_position-indicating_radiobeacon_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Emergency position-indicating radiobeacon station">Emergency position-indicating radiobeacon station</a></span></p>
Tracking transmitters which aid in the detection and location of boats and people in distress at sea.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="emergency_swimming_ascent" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">emergency swimming ascent</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "ESA", "Controlled emergency swimming ascent", "CESA"</span></p>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Emergency_swimming_ascent" class="mw-redirect" title="Emergency swimming ascent">Emergency swimming ascent</a></span></p>
Emergency procedure where the diver makes an ascent at approximately neutral buoyancy from depth after a breathing gas supply failure.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="encapsulation" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">encapsulation</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Using a diving suit which completely isolates the diver from direct contact with the environment.<sup id="cite_ref-encapsulation_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-encapsulation-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="end" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">END</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#equivalent_Narcotic_Depth"><span title="See entry on this page at § Equivalent Narcotic Depth" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">Equivalent Narcotic Depth</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="enriched_air_nitrox" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Enriched Air Nitrox</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <span title="See entry on this page at § nitrox" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O#nitrox" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: H–O">nitrox</a></span></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="epirb" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">EPIRB</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#emergency_position_indicating_radio_beacon"><span title="See entry on this page at § emergency position indicating radio beacon" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">emergency position indicating radio beacon</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="equalise" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">equalise</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Balance pressure of a gas filled space with the ambient pressure, by adding or venting gas, to prevent barotrauma or pressure damage.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="equivalent_air_depth" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">equivalent air depth</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "EAD"</span></p>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Equivalent_air_depth" title="Equivalent air depth">Equivalent air depth</a></span></p>
Depth at which partial pressure of nitrogen in a <a href="/wiki/Nitrox" title="Nitrox">nitrox</a> mixture at a given depth is equal to the partial pressure of nitrogen in air. Used for approximating the <a href="/wiki/Decompression_(diving)" title="Decompression (diving)">decompression</a> requirements of nitrox mixtures by finding the depth at which air would require the same decompression. Based on exposure to equal partial pressures of nitrogen at maximum depth.<sup id="cite_ref-USNDM_R6_3-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USNDM_R6-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="equivalent_narcotic_depth" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">equivalent narcotic depth</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="equivalent_nitrogen_depth" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">equivalent nitrogen depth</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "END"</span></p>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Equivalent_narcotic_depth" title="Equivalent narcotic depth">Equivalent narcotic depth</a></span></p>
A way of expressing the narcotic effect of a breathing gas mixture at depth by comparison with the depth at which air would have a similar effect. Used to choose nitrogen content of a Trimix breathing gas for a planned dive profile to limit <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen_narcosis" title="Nitrogen narcosis">nitrogen narcosis</a>. Based on limiting the partial pressure of nitrogen during the dive by diluting the breathing gas with helium.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="escr" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">eSCR</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Electronic semi-closed circuit rebreather, where an electronic control system monitors the partial pressure of oxygen and adds gas to maintain a <a href="#floating_setpoint"><span title="See entry on this page at § floating setpoint" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">floating setpoint</span></a> to optimise gas use and compensate for variations in diver exertion.<sup id="cite_ref-Heinerth_9-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heinerth-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="european_diving_technology_committee" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">European Diving Technology Committee</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/European_Diving_Technology_Committee" title="European Diving Technology Committee">European Diving Technology Committee</a></span></p>
International committee of European representatives promoting good standards for diving and co-ordinating, where possible, differing standards with the aim of making European professional diving safer.<sup id="cite_ref-EDTC_2017_2-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EDTC_2017-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EDTC_2010_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EDTC_2010-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="exceptional_exposure" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">exceptional exposure</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A dive in which the risk of decompresssion sickness, oxygen toxicity, and/or exposure to the elements is substantially greater than on a normal working dive.<sup id="cite_ref-USNDMR6_9-3.23_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USNDMR6_9-3.23-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="excursion" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">excursion</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="excursion_dive" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">excursion dive</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Saturation diving where the divers work at a depth deeper or shallower than the saturation depth, after which they are returned to the original saturation pressure.<sup id="cite_ref-EDTC_2017_2-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EDTC_2017-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="excursion_tables" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">excursion tables</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Tables for use in saturation diving that specify the limit upward and downward of excursions from the nominal depth, and provide a zone in which the diver can move freely without regard to the number of excursions or their duration without incurring a decompression penalty.<sup id="cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_8-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="excursion_umbilical" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">excursion umbilical</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Umbilical_cable#Diver" title="Umbilical cable">Umbilical cable#Diver</a></span></p>
The combined supply and return hoses and cables for life-line, life-support, heating, power and communications between a diving bell and the diver</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="exhaust_valve" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">exhaust valve</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A valve controlling the venting of gas from any higher pressure source such as a diving chamber, diver’s helmet, dry suit, buoyancy system, volume tank, lift bag etc. For some of these applications, also known as a <a href="#dump_valve"><span title="See entry on this page at § dump valve" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">dump valve</span></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_8-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="extraction_ratio" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">extraction ratio</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "ventilation/oxygen extraction ratio"</span></p>
Ratio between minute ventilation and oxygen uptake, the volume rate of gas breathed to the amount of oxygen taken up in the bloodstream. A typical surface extraction ratio of 20 would mean that for every 20 litres of gas breathed, 1 litre of oxygen would be absorbed in the lungs.</dd>

</dl>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Fa">Fa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Fa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<dl class="glossary">

<dt class="glossary" id="faceplate" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">faceplate</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><span title="See entry on this page at § viewport" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_T%E2%80%93Z#viewport" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: T–Z">Viewport</a></span> of a full-face mask or helmet. The transparent window through which the diver can see the surroundings.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="failure_modes_and_effects_analysis" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">failure modes and effects analysis</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "FMEA"</span></p>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Failure_mode_and_effects_analysis" title="Failure mode and effects analysis">Failure mode and effects analysis</a></span></p>
A methodology used to identify potential failure modes, determine their effects and identify actions to mitigate the potential failures.<sup id="cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_8-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="failure_modes,_effects,_and_criticality_analysis" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">failure modes, effects, and criticality analysis</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "FMECA"</span></p>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Failure_mode,_effects_and_criticality_analysis" class="mw-redirect" title="Failure mode, effects and criticality analysis">Failure mode, effects and criticality analysis</a></span></p>
An extension to FMEA of a criticality analysis, which combines the probability of failure modes with the severity of their consequences to identify relative risk of each mode, allowing remedial effort to be directed where it is likely to produce the greatest effect.<sup id="cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_8-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="farmer_john" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">farmer john</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><a href="/wiki/Wet_suit" class="mw-redirect" title="Wet suit">Wet suit</a> that covers the torso and legs only; it resembles a <a href="/wiki/Bib_overall" class="mw-redirect" title="Bib overall">bib overall</a> or <a href="/wiki/Salopettes" class="mw-redirect" title="Salopettes">salopettes</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fatigue_cracking" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">fatigue cracking</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Fatigue_(material)" title="Fatigue (material)">Fatigue (material)</a></span></p>
Cracking in a material resulting from multiple stress cycles below the ultimate or yield strength. Usually refers to large number of cycles.</dd>

</dl>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Fe">Fe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Fe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<dl class="glossary">

<dt class="glossary" id="feather_breathing" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">feather breathing</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Sidemount_diving#Skills" title="Sidemount diving">Sidemount diving#Skills</a></span></p>
Technique for emergency breathing from a free-flowing demand valve where the diver manually controls air flow by opening and closing the cylinder valve.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="feet_sea_water" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">feet sea water</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Feet_sea_water" class="mw-redirect" title="Feet sea water">feet sea water</a></span></p>
Unit of pressure equal to 1/33 atm. Not a linear measure of depth. Generally defined as the pressure exerted by a foot depth of seawater having a specific gravity of 1.027 and is approximately equal to 0.445 pounds per square inch.<sup id="cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_8-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="ffm" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">FFM</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#full-face_mask"><span title="See entry on this page at § full-face mask" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">full-face mask</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="ffw" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">ffw</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="ffw" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">FFW</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Feet_fresh_water" class="mw-redirect" title="Feet fresh water">Feet fresh water</a></span></p>
Feet fresh water. Unit of pressure equal to 1/34 atm. Not a linear measure of depth.</dd>
</dl>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Fi">Fi</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Fi">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt class="glossary" id="filling_ratio" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">filling ratio</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Ratio of the mass of gas in a cylinder to the internal volume of the cylinder (water capacity), usually expressed in kilograms per litre, or pounds per cubic foot.<sup id="cite_ref-SANS10019:2019_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SANS10019:2019-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="filling_whip" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">filling whip</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Diving_air_compressor#Filling_diving_cylinders" title="Diving air compressor">Diving air compressor#Filling diving cylinders</a> and <a href="/wiki/Diving_cylinder#Filling" title="Diving cylinder">Diving cylinder#Filling</a></span></p>
High pressure flexible hose used to connect a cylinder to the storage cylinder, filling panel, booster or compressor, through which high pressure gas flows to fill the cylinder.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="filtration" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">filtration</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Filtration" title="Filtration">Filtration</a></span></p>
Process for removing impurities from a fluid. Particulates are commonly removed by passing the fluid through porous material with pore size small enough to trap the particles (e.g. micron filters). Liquids and gases are commonly absorbed or adsorbed by the surface of the filter medium (e.g. activated carbon, molecular sieve, silica gel), or may be chemically combined with the medium (e.g. Sodalime) or catalytically converted (e.g. Hopcalite) into a less objectionable substance.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fin_keepers" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">fin keepers</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="fin_retainers" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">fin retainers</dfn></dt> 
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "fin holders", "fin fasteners", "fin grips", "fin keeps", "fin guards", "flipper fixers", "Y-straps", "ankle straps", "accessory safety straps", "fix fins", "grip fins" and, in recognition of their French origin, "fixe-palmes".</span></p>
<p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Swimfin#Attachment" title="Swimfin">Swimfin#Attachment</a></span></p>
Y-shaped elastic rubber straps worn over the arch, the heel and the instep of each foot to help prevent swim-fins from falling off the diver's feet. Mainly used with full-foot-pocket fins.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="first_stage" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">first stage</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Diving_regulator#First_stage" title="Diving regulator">Diving regulator#First stage</a></span></p>
Diving regulator component which reduces gas pressure from storage pressure in the cylinder to interstage pressure for supply to the second stage and for suit and buoyancy compensator inflation.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="five_nines" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">five nines</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="five_nines_purity" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">five nines purity</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">99.999% pure gas. Usually referring to <a href="/wiki/Breathing_gas" title="Breathing gas">breathing grade</a> oxygen or helium for blending.<sup id="cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_1-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fixed_diving_system" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">fixed diving system</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A <a href="#diving_system"><span title="See entry on this page at § diving system" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">diving system</span></a> (q.v.) installed permanently on a vessel or structure.<sup id="cite_ref-IMCA_D_057_8-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMCA_D_057-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="floating_setpoint" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">floating setpoint</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#dynamic_setpoint"><span title="See entry on this page at § dynamic setpoint" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">dynamic setpoint</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="flood-up_valve" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">flood-up valve</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: bell flooding valve<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup></span></p>
A valve in a <a href="/wiki/Diving_bell" title="Diving bell">diving bell</a> which allows air to escape and internal water level to rise. This can be useful to assist the <span title="See entry on this page at § bellman" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#bellman" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C">bellman</a></span> in recovering an incapacitated diver through the bottom hatch.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="flow" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">flow</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Movement of water through a cave or ducting system. Similar in meaning to current in open water.<sup id="cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_1-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fluorocarbon_elastomers" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">fluorocarbon elastomers</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main: <a href="/wiki/Fluoroelastomer" title="Fluoroelastomer">Fluoroelastomer</a></span></p>
Synthetic elastomers (rubber) with good performance in high partial pressures of oxygen. Preferred material for o-rings in diving regulators for <a href="/wiki/Oxygen_service" class="mw-redirect" title="Oxygen service">oxygen service</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="flush" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">flush</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#diluent_flush"><span title="See entry on this page at § diluent flush" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">diluent flush</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="flutter_kick" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">flutter kick</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Finning_techniques#Flutter_kick" title="Finning techniques">Finning techniques#Flutter kick</a></span></p>
finning style where the fins are alternately moved up and down by movements of the full leg.<sup id="cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_1-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Thrust is developed on both up and down strokes. Vortices shed move both upwards and downwards. See also <span title="See entry on this page at § modified flutter kick" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O#modified_flutter_kick" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: H–O">modified flutter kick</a></span>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fmea" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">FMEA</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#failure_modes_and_effects_analysis"><span title="See entry on this page at § failure modes and effects analysis" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">failure modes and effects analysis</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="fmeca" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">FMECA</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#failure_modes,_effects_and_criticality_analysis"><span title="See entry on this page at § failure modes, effects and criticality analysis" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">failure modes, effects and criticality analysis</span></a></span></p></dd>
</dl>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Fo">Fo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Fo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt class="glossary" id="fogging" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">fogging</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Anti-fog" title="Anti-fog">Anti-fog</a></span></p>
Condensation of water vapour on the inside surface of a mask or helmet faceplate, reducing visibility.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="forward_roll_entry" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">forward roll entry</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Scuba_skills#Entries" title="Scuba skills">Scuba skills#Entries</a></span></p>
Water entry technique used by scuba divers from a boat or platform too high or unsuitable for <span title="See entry on this page at § backward roll entry" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#backward_roll_entry" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C">backward roll entry</a></span>. The diver bends forward at the hips and waist and falls forward into the water, making a partial somersault and breaking the water with the cylinder, back and shoulders. Not suitable for heights more than about 2&#160;m, and can be problematic if the diver is carrying several heavy items like stage cylinders or large cameras.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="four-wire_system" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">four-wire system</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Voice communications using separate wire pairs for each direction.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="frame" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">frame</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Transportable assemblies of gas cylinders connected by a manifold and securely mounted to a structural framework.<sup id="cite_ref-Bevan_2005_21-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bevan_2005-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> See also <span title="See entry on this page at § quad" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#quad" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S">quad</a></span> and <span title="See entry on this page at § kelly" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O#kelly" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: H–O">kelly</a></span>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="free_air" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">free air</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See also: <a href="#free_gas"><span title="See entry on this page at § free gas" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">free gas</span></a></span></p>
Air at normal atmospheric pressure.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="free-diving" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">free-diving</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Free-diving" class="mw-redirect" title="Free-diving">Free-diving</a></span></p>
Underwater diving that does not involve the use of external breathing apparatus, but relies on a diver's ability to hold their breath until resurfacing. See also <span title="See entry on this page at § breath-hold diving" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#breath-hold_diving" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C">breath-hold diving</a></span>, and <span title="See entry on this page at § apnea" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#apnea" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C">apnea</a></span> (q.v.)</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="free-flow" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">free-flow</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;Constant flow rate air supply</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;See: <a href="/wiki/Mechanism_of_diving_regulators#Free-flow" title="Mechanism of diving regulators">Mechanism of diving regulators#Free-flow</a> <br />
Malfunction of a demand regulator where the valve sticks in the open position, causing a continuous flow.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="free-flow_helmet" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">free-flow helmet</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Diving_helmet#Free-flow_helmets" title="Diving helmet">Diving helmet#Free-flow helmets</a></span></p>
A helmet where the breathing air supply is supplied at an adjustable, but approximately constant rate regardless of the diver's instantaneous breathing rate.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="free-flow_valve" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">free-flow valve</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Valve on the side of a <a href="#demand_helmet"><span title="See entry on this page at § demand helmet" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">demand helmet</span></a> or full-face mask which opens a continuous flow of breathing gas into the helmet interior, usually directed over the interior of the viewport, hence alternative term defogging valve, as it is often used to blow condensation from the inside of the viewport.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="free_gas" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">free gas</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Gas at normal atmospheric pressure. Usually refers to the volume of some amount of compressed gas when allowed to expand to atmospheric pressure at constant temperature</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="free_gas_volume" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">free gas volume</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Equivalent volume of a compressed gas if expanded to  standard atmospheric pressure at constant temperature.<sup id="cite_ref-engineering_toolbox_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-engineering_toolbox-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="frenzel_maneuver" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Frenzel maneuver</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ear_clearing" title="Ear clearing">Ear clearing</a></span></p>
Technique for equalising the middle ear by pinching the nose closed and moving the back of the tongue upwards.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="frog_kick" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">frog kick</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Frog_kick" class="mw-redirect" title="Frog kick">Frog kick</a></span></p>
Finning technique where thrust is developed by sweeping the fins horizontally toward each other with the fins twisted into a nearly vertical plane, with the soles facing each other, followed by a recovery stroke which develops negligible thrust where the fin blades are feathered. The legs are fairly straight during the power stroke. See also: <span title="See entry on this page at § modified frog kick" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O#modified_frog_kick" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: H–O">modified frog kick</a></span>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="frogman" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">frogman</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Frogman" title="Frogman">Frogman</a></span></p>
A scuba diver, particularly a military diver on an undercover mission.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="fsw" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">fsw</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#feet_sea_water"><span title="See entry on this page at § feet sea water" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">feet sea water</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="full_duplex" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">full duplex</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Duplex_(telecommunications)#Full_duplex" title="Duplex (telecommunications)">Duplex (telecommunications)#Full duplex</a></span></p>
Voice communication system where both users can transmit and receive at the same time. Compare with <a href="#full_duplex">half duplex</a></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="full-face_mask" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">full-face mask</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Full-face_diving_mask" title="Full-face diving mask">Full-face diving mask</a></span></p>
Diving mask covering the eyes, nose and mouth, and which provides the diver with breathing gas</dd>

</dl>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="G">G</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: G">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ga">Ga</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Ga">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<dl class="glossary">

<dt class="glossary" id="gap" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gap</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See also: <span title="See entry on this page at § jump" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O#jump" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: H–O">jump</a></span></span></p> 
The space between two cave guidelines. Usually between a main guideline and the start tie-off of a branch line.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gap_spool" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gap spool</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Distance_line#Spools" title="Distance line">Distance line#Spools</a></span></p>
A relatively short length of cave line on a spool used to bridge a gap between lines when making an excursion from the main guideline to a branch guideline. The line is left in place during the excursion, and usually retrieved on the way out</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gaiter" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gaiter</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "gator" (US)</span></p> Textile legging wrapped around the calf and ankle area over a dry suit to restrict the amount of air that can get into the lower leg area. Also can reduce drag of the suit in this area by smoothing over creases and folds.</dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="gas_blender" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gas blender</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;Person who mixes breathing gases for diving, filling <a href="/wiki/Diving_cylinder" title="Diving cylinder">diving cylinders</a> with gas mixes such as <a href="/wiki/Nitrox" title="Nitrox">nitrox</a> or <a href="/wiki/Trimix_(breathing_gas)" title="Trimix (breathing gas)">trimix</a>.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;Certification of competence to mix breathing gases for diving.<sup id="cite_ref-ISO13293_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ISO13293-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gas_blending" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gas blending</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Gas_blending_for_scuba_diving" title="Gas blending for scuba diving">Gas blending for scuba diving</a></span></p>
Mixing breathing gases for diving, filling <a href="/wiki/Diving_cylinder" title="Diving cylinder">diving cylinders</a> with gas mixes such as <a href="/wiki/Nitrox" title="Nitrox">nitrox</a> or <a href="/wiki/Trimix_(breathing_gas)" title="Trimix (breathing gas)">trimix</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gas_block" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gas block</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#gas_switching_block"><span title="See entry on this page at § gas switching block" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">gas switching block</span></a></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="gas_embolism" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gas embolism</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Gas_embolism" class="mw-redirect" title="Gas embolism">Gas embolism</a></span></p>
Blockage of a blood vessel by a bubble of gas.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gas_extender" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gas extender</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Carbon dioxide scrubber used to allow partial recirculation of surface-supplied or scuba breathing gas to reduce waste. A form of <a href="/wiki/Rebreather#Semi-closed_circuit_rebreathers" title="Rebreather">semi-closed circuit rebreather</a>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gaseous_impurities" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gaseous impurities</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Contaminants in the compressed breathing air or gas mixture which are in gaseous form. Compare with particulate and condensate impurities.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gas_integration" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gas integration</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="gas-integrated_dive_computer" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">gas-integrated dive computer</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Gas-integrated_dive_computer" class="mw-redirect" title="Gas-integrated dive computer">Gas-integrated dive computer</a></span></p>
Technology to display gas pressure in a scuba cylinder on a dive computer, and in some cases make further use of the information for gas management.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gas_fraction" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gas fraction</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Gas_composition" title="Gas composition">Gas composition</a></span></p>
The fraction by molecular count, volume or pressure (they all come to the same thing) of a specific gas in a mixture of gases.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gas_matching" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gas matching</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Scuba_gas_planning#Gas_matching" title="Scuba gas planning">Scuba gas planning#Gas matching</a></span></p>
The calculation of reserve and turn pressures for divers using different cylinder volumes on the same dive, allowing each diver to ensure that sufficient gas is retained at all times to allow for foreseeable contingencies based on each diver's cylinder volumes, and both divers' individual gas consumption rates.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gas_narcosis" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gas narcosis</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <span title="See entry on this page at § inert gas narcosis" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O#inert_gas_narcosis" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: H–O">inert gas narcosis</a></span></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="gas_panel" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gas panel</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Surface-supplied_diving#Gas_panel" title="Surface-supplied diving">Surface-supplied diving#Gas panel</a></span></p>
The control equipment for providing breathing gas to surface supplied divers via umbilicals. Primary and reserve gas is supplied to the panel through shutoff valves from low pressure compressors or high pressure storage cylinders.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gas_reversal_point" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gas reversal point</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The depth during an ascent or decompression when the intake of dissolved gas is exceeded by outgassing.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gas_sensor" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gas sensor</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A component that produces a signal in the presence of a specific gas, often in proportion to the concentration of the gas.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gas_switching" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gas switching</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Gas_switching" class="mw-redirect" title="Gas switching">Gas switching</a></span></p>
The procedure of changing from one breathing gas mixture to another during a dive. This may be done to avoid oxygen toxicity, hypoxia, or nitrogen narcosis, to accelerate decompression, or to avoid running out of breathing gas. Generally applied to open circuit breathing equipment, where a physical change-over of gas source is made. In closed circuit systems the gas composition is continuously controlled to follow the chosen <span title="See entry on this page at § set-point" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#set-point" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S">set-point</a></span>.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gas_switching_block" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gas switching block</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A valve set used for switching from one breathing gas to another during a dive. The most common application is a <span title="See entry on this page at § bailout block" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_A%E2%80%93C#bailout_block" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: A–C">bailout block</a></span>, but also used to switch gases for decompression on a full face mask, and to switch between deep and shallow gases on a semi-closed rebreather.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gauge_mode" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gauge mode</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Dive_computer#Additional_functionality_and_features" title="Dive computer">Dive computer#Additional functionality and features</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dive_computer#Management_of_violations" title="Dive computer">Dive computer#Management of violations</a></span></p>
Operating mode for a personal dive computer where the decompression calculation is disabled, and the unit operated only as a timer and depth gauge. Typically used when diving with gas mixtures not supported by the algorithm, in which case decompression tables are used to monitor and control the decompression schedule. Some dive computers will automatically switch to gauge mode if the diver violates a depth limit, leaving the diver without decompression information.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gauge_pressure" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gauge pressure</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Pressure_measurement#Absolute,_gauge_and_differential_pressures_-_zero_reference" title="Pressure measurement">Pressure measurement#Absolute, gauge and differential pressures - zero reference</a></span></p>
Gauge pressure is zero-referenced against ambient air pressure, so it is equal to absolute pressure minus atmospheric pressure</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gauge_snubber" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gauge snubber</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A <a href="/wiki/Needle_valve" title="Needle valve">needle valve</a> or small bore orifice between the pressure supply and the gauge which damps pressure fluctuations.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gay-lussac&#39;s_law" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Gay-Lussac's law</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Gay-Lussac%27s_law" title="Gay-Lussac&#39;s law">Gay-Lussac's law</a></span></p>
Relation between temperature and pressure in an ideal gas for a constant volume.</dd>
</dl>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ge">Ge</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Ge">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt class="glossary" id="general_gas_equation" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">general gas equation</dfn></dt>
<dt class="glossary" id="general_gas_law" style="margin-top: -0.2em;"><dfn class="glossary">general gas law</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">1.&#160;&#160;Relation between the variables pressure, volume and temperature for a given mass of a given mixture of an ideal gas.</dd>
<dd class="glossary">2.&#160;&#160;Thermodynamic equation of state for gases for the variables volume, pressure, temperature and number and atomic weight of molecules.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="giant_stride_entry" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">giant stride entry</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <span title="See entry on this page at § stride entry" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_P%E2%80%93S#stride_entry" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: P–S">stride entry</a></span></span></p></dd>
<dt class="glossary" id="glossopharangeal_insufflation" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">glossopharangeal insufflation</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Also: "buccal pumping", "lung packing"</span></p>
A method used by <a href="/wiki/Freediving" title="Freediving">freedivers</a> for filling the lungs with more air than maximal inspiration to normal total lung capacity (TLC). After a full inhalation, the diver fills the mouth with air, while the glottis remains closed, then opens the glottis and forces this air into the lung using the cheeks and tongue to reduce the mouth volume. This may be repeated several times.<sup id="cite_ref-Potkin_et_al_2007_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Potkin_et_al_2007-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="glowstick" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">glowstick</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A single-use, translucent plastic tube containing isolated substances that, when combined, make light through chemiluminescence</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gnarly" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gnarly</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A general purpose adjective to denote a particularly difficult section of a cave, which may be low, tight, silty, etc. or a combination.<sup id="cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_1-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>
</dl>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Go">Go</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_D%E2%80%93G&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Go">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<dl class="glossary">
<dt class="glossary" id="go_into_decompression" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">go into decompression</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">Incur a decompression obligation. Generally refers to having a theoretical tissue inert gas concentration that requires the diver to make staged decompression stops during ascent to avoid an unacceptable risk of symptomatic decompression sickness according to the decompression model, algorithm, tables or dive computer in use.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="golden_rule" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">golden rule</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The convention in cave diving that anyone can turn the dive at any time for any reason.<sup id="cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_1-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gold_line" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gold line</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">The permanent main guideline in a cave system, that usually starts well inside the cave. Often yellow or gold in colour.<sup id="cite_ref-Cave_diving_terms_1-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cave_diving_terms-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="goodman_handle" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">Goodman handle</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary">A handle used to carry the primary dive light head comprising a rigid slot through which the fingers and palm of the hand are extended, so that the light rests on the back of the hand, facing the direction of the extended fingers.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gps" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">GPS</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Global_Positioning_System" title="Global Positioning System">Global Positioning System</a></span></p>
A satellite navigation system that provides location and time information in all weather, anywhere on or near the Earth, where there is an unobstructed line of sight to four or more GPS satellites</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="gradient_factor" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">gradient factor</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="/wiki/Decompression_theory#Gradient_factors" title="Decompression theory">Decompression theory#Gradient factors</a></span></p>
A way of modifying the <span title="See entry on this page at § M-value" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id=""><a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_underwater_diving_terminology:_H%E2%80%93O#M-value" title="Glossary of underwater diving terminology: H–O">M-values</a></span> of a decompression algorithm to more conservative values in proportion to depth. Often used to bias the algorithm towards deeper stops by using a smaller value for the deeper value.</dd>

<dt class="glossary" id="guide_line" style="margin-top: 0.4em;"><dfn class="glossary">guide line</dfn></dt>
<dd class="glossary"><p class="glossary-hatnote"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"/><span role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">See: <a href="#distance_line"><span title="See entry on this page at § distance line" class="glossary-link-internal" style="border-bottom: 1px dashed #86a1ff; color:initial;" id="">distance line</span></a></span></p></dd>
